<p>The discography of <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">Pink Floyd</a>, a British rock band, consists of fifteen <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Studio_album" title="Studio album">studio albums</a>, three <a href="/wiki/Live_album" title="Live album">live albums</a>, eight <a href="/wiki/Compilation_album" title="Compilation album">compilation albums</a>, four <a href="/wiki/Box_set" title="Box set">box sets</a>, four <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Video_album" title="Video album">video albums</a>, one <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">extended play</a> and twenty-seven <a href="/wiki/Single_(music)" title="Single (music)">singles</a>.</p>
<p>Formed in 1965, Pink Floyd initially earned recognition for their <a href="/wiki/Psychedelic_rock" title="Psychedelic rock">psychedelic</a> or <a href="/wiki/Space_rock" title="Space rock">space rock</a> music, and, as they evolved, for their <a href="/wiki/Progressive_rock" title="Progressive rock">progressive rock</a> music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allmusic_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusic-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> They are known for <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">philosophical</a> lyrics, <a href="/wiki/Acoustics" title="Acoustics">sonic experimentation</a>, innovative <a href="/wiki/Cover_art" title="Cover art">cover art</a>, and elaborate <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd_live_performances" title="Pink Floyd live performances">live shows</a>. One of rock music's most successful acts, the group have sold over 250 million albums worldwide,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> including 74.5 million units sold in the United States alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-e_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-e-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>As a psychedelic band led by <a href="/wiki/Syd_Barrett" title="Syd Barrett">Syd Barrett</a> in the late 1960s, Pink Floyd had moderate mainstream success and were one of the most popular bands in the <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a> underground music scene;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> however, Barrett's erratic behaviour eventually forced his colleagues to replace him with guitarist and singer <a href="/wiki/David_Gilmour" title="David Gilmour">David Gilmour</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allmusic_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusic-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> After Barrett's departure, the band released <i><a href="/wiki/Ummagumma" title="Ummagumma">Ummagumma</a></i>. The album was released as a double disc, the first disc containing songs performed live, the second containing new studio-recorded songs. Singer and bass player <a href="/wiki/Roger_Waters" title="Roger Waters">Roger Waters</a> gradually became the dominant and driving force in the mid-1970s, until his departure from the group in 1985.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allmusic_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusic-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> The band recorded several <a href="/wiki/Album" title="Album">albums</a>, achieving worldwide success with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Side_of_the_Moon" title="The Dark Side of the Moon">The Dark Side of the Moon</a></i> (1973), <i><a href="/wiki/Wish_You_Were_Here_(Pink_Floyd_album)" title="Wish You Were Here (Pink Floyd album)">Wish You Were Here</a></i> (1975), <i><a href="/wiki/Animals_(Pink_Floyd_album)" title="Animals (Pink Floyd album)">Animals</a></i> (1977), and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall" title="The Wall">The Wall</a></i> (1979); all except <i>Animals</i> reached number one in the US. <i>The Dark Side of the Moon</i> is one of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_albums_worldwide" title="List of best-selling albums worldwide">best-selling albums in the world</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Floyds_Dark_Side_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Floyds_Dark_Side-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> and <i>The Wall</i> is the highest-certified multiple-disc album by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1986, Waters declared Pink Floyd "a spent force" and sued to dissolve their partnership and retire the name Pink Floyd, but the remaining members, led by Gilmour, continued recording and touring under the name Pink Floyd.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Allmusic_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-Allmusic-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> Following an out-of-court settlement, the band enjoyed worldwide success with <i><a href="/wiki/A_Momentary_Lapse_of_Reason" title="A Momentary Lapse of Reason">A Momentary Lapse of Reason</a></i> (1987), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Division_Bell" title="The Division Bell">The Division Bell</a></i> (1994) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Endless_River" title="The Endless River">The Endless River</a></i> (2014).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-schaffner_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-schaffner-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Pink_Floyd_discography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="refbegin" style="">
<ul>
<li><b>A</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_a1"><b><a href="#ref_note_a1">^</a></b></span> <i>Delicate Sound of Thunder</i> did not enter the Canadian Albums Chart, but peaked at number seven on the Long Form Music Videos chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>B</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_b1"><b><a href="#ref_note_b1">^</a></b></span> "See Emily Play" did not enter the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, but peaked at number 134 on the <a href="/wiki/Bubbling_Under_Hot_100_Singles" title="Bubbling Under Hot 100 Singles">Bubbling Under Hot 100 Singles</a> chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>C</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_c1"><b><a href="#ref_note_c1">^</a></b></span> "Us and Them" did not enter the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, but peaked at number 101 on the Bubbling Under Hot 100 Singles chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</div>
